It is explained in many places that there are two levels in the *mochin* (intellects)—the externality of the *mochin* and the internality of the *mochin*. The difference between them is: even though the brain rules over the heart, and contemplation of the greatness of Hashem gives birth in the heart to the love of Hashem and His awe (as explained in the Rambam), there is a difference between the externality of the intellect and the internality of the intellect in the manner of their influence on the *middos* in the heart:

The influence of the externality of the intellect on the *middos* is by way of action. After the person understands and grasps in his intellect the greatness of Hashem ("and you shall know"), there must be an additional service to bring about the birth of a *middah* in the heart ("and you shall return to your heart"), which comes through a special engagement on the part of the intellect in the head, to be clothed in the "world of *middos*" and to awaken the feeling in the heart. It is understood that regarding the level of the intellect itself, this is a descent.

This is not so for the influence of the internality of the intellect, which is connected with the essence of the soul; it is in all parts of the person by way of "automatically," for the grasping of something from the side of the internality of the intellect is in a way that the person is attached to it with his entire existence, in a way that the *middos* are dragged automatically after the grasping.

This is the difference between the two modes in arm-tefillin and head-tefillin:

### 29

At the beginning of the service, when the service of the intellect is only at the level of externality, then arm-tefillin and head-tefillin are two mitzvos, meaning that they are two different services, the service of the heart and the service of the brain, and they are also distinct in their level, for the subjugation of the brain to the service of Hashem is in a constant manner, "that it be placed," whereas the awakening of the *middos* is by way of action, that through the brain he binds his heart to Hashem.

This is not so when he ascends in his service, until his service is from the side of the internality of the *mochin*; then the *middos* are dragged automatically after the intellect (as mentioned above), and then arm-tefillin and head-tefillin are one mitzvah, and the *middos* are secondary to the service of the *mochin* and are dragged after it, "as long as they are between your eyes, there must be two."


## תבא (תנש"א)

## 37

### Tavo (5751)

1. "Rabbi Yochanan said: There are three keys in the hand of the Holy One, Blessed be He, which were not entrusted to any messenger. They are: the key of rain, the key of childbirth, and the key of the resurrection of the dead. The key of rain, as it is written: 'Hashem will open for you His good treasure, the heavens, to give the rain of your land in its time...' In the West [Eretz Yisrael], they say: also the key of sustenance, as it is written: 'You open Your hand, etc.' And Rabbi Yochanan, what is his reason for not counting this? He would say to you: Rain is also sustenance."

Seemingly, it appears that Rabbi Yochanan is speaking in general terms, and that in a general sense, "rain is also sustenance," as Rashi explains: "For seeds and fruits grow from them (from the rains) for the sustenance of the world." In the West, they are more specific, and therefore they counted "sustenance" as a separate key. Even though, in a general sense, rains are the source of the world's sustenance, nevertheless, because specifically there is sustenance that does not come through rain (and conversely, there are rains that do not directly relate to sustenance, as they do not descend in the proper measure for seeds and fruits to grow from them), they therefore counted "sustenance" separately.

However, the style of the Gemara does not imply this: "And Rabbi Yochanan, what is his reason for not counting this? He would say to you, etc." The plain meaning of the language indicates that there is a disagreement here and that these are two different opinions on the matter.

2. This can be explained by clarifying the reasoning behind the disagreement, after first answering the question raised by the commentators regarding Rabbi Yochanan’s statement, "He would say to you: Rain is also sustenance." For Rabbi Yochanan himself says later: "Rain is for an individual, sustenance is for the many. Rain is for an individual, as it is written: 'Hashem will open for you His good treasure to give the rain of your land.' Sustenance is for the many, as it is written: 'Behold, I will rain down bread for you.'" This shows that even according to Rabbi Yochanan, rain and sustenance are two different things.

It can be said, based on what Rashi writes in his commentary on the Gemara there: "Rain is for an individual—if one needs rain only for one person, for example, if he planted after the general planting time, or if he lives in a city of non-Jews and needs rain, it comes in his merit. But sustenance—an abundance of good and life for the entire world—does not come to the world in the merit of one person, but only for the many. If many need plenty, and they merit it, the Holy One, Blessed be He, sends a blessing upon the grain. But for an individual who needs his crops to be blessed, the Holy One, Blessed be He, does not change the law of the year for him, but only according to its blessings. Even though He brings down rain for an individual to improve his crops so they are not worse than others, He does not make his field like a field of plenty."

According to this, it is understood that the intention of "sustenance" there is a special abundance that is in the manner of "plenty." If so, it is understood that only in this manner are sustenance and rain two different things.

In the *Chiddushei Aggados* of the Maharsha there, he explains: "Rain is only a necessity for sustenance, and it is given by nature from the heavens; if there is a need for an individual, it is given to him in his merit. But sustenance itself, in the sense of it coming from the heavens—such as the *Man* and the well—is a miraculous thing and comes only for the many."

Based on this, one could explain the difference between the opinion of Rabbi Yochanan and those in the West: Rabbi Yochanan, who says "Rain is also sustenance," is speaking of regular sustenance, not in the manner of special "plenty," and not sustenance that comes in a revealed way from Above. Whereas those in the West, who count sustenance as a separate key, are referring to sustenance that is a special influence from the Holy One, Blessed be He, which comes only for the many.

However, according to this, the Gemara’s question still remains: "And Rabbi Yochanan, what is his reason for not counting this?" That is, why did Rabbi Yochanan count only the sustenance that is included in rain (and there are only three keys), and not also count this key of sustenance that is not included in "rain," which is a separate key that comes from Hashem and was not entrusted to a messenger?

3. Therefore, it seems to me that Rabbi Yochanan and those in the West are both speaking about the same type of "sustenance," but they disagree on the logic of whether "sustenance" requires a special "key," or if it is included in the "key" of rain.

The explanation is as follows:
"Rain" and "sustenance" are generally descriptors for the influence of food and human needs. The difference between them is that "rain" denotes the influence of sustenance from Above—"I will give your rains in their time"—whereas the term "sustenance" generally describes the reception of that influence, that the person is sustained and nourished by this influence. This is also the simple understanding: "rain" comes from Above and causes growth, etc., whereas "sustenance" comes through the work and action of the person—plowing, sowing, and harvesting, etc.

According to this, the difference between Rabbi Yochanan and those in the West is that Rabbi Yochanan speaks of the "keys" of things as they come from the Holy One, Blessed be He, the Giver. Therefore, he counts only "rain" and not sustenance (for sustenance is not the influence of the Holy One, Blessed be He, from His side, but rather the work of the person so that the influence of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is received by him). Whereas those in the West speak also as it is from the side of the receiver, as the influence of food becomes "sustenance," and therefore they also counted "sustenance."

[According to this explanation, the correspondence to the number of keys is also understood: according to Rabbi Yochanan, there are three keys, and according to the West, there are four: The difference between the letter *gimel* and the letter *dalet* is (as it is in the Gemara)—"gemul dalim" (rewarding the poor). That is, the letter *gimel* indicates the source of the influence, the "One who bestows kindness," and the letter *dalet* indicates the "poor," the receivers of the influence. From this, it is also understood regarding the *gematria* of these letters—the number three and the number four—that the number three indicates the giving, as it is from the side of the Giver ("bestower"), while four indicates it as it is from the side of the receiver (the "poor").]

4. However, it still requires explanation, for the content explained in this *sugya* is about "keys in the hand of the Holy One, Blessed be He, which were not entrusted to a messenger." That is, the definition of these "keys" is that they all come from the Holy One, Blessed be He, and there is no "intermediary" in the middle. If so, what is the meaning of "In the West they say: also the key of sustenance," that they counted "sustenance" as a separate key because sustenance is a matter that depends on and relates to human work (and therefore it is not a detail in the key of "rain")—according to this, how can it be said that this is a "key" that is only in the hand of the Holy One, Blessed be He?

This can be explained by first noting what our Sages explained regarding the descent of rain, which comes from Above: one of the reasons for this is "so that everyone will keep their eyes turned upward." Meaning, the fact that the sustenance of the creatures depends on rain that comes from Above and not on something that is in the hands of the person himself to do (like in the land of Egypt, where the irrigation of the fields is "by your foot"), works in them the proper recognition that all their sustenance and vitality (and not just the rain) is through the Holy One, Blessed be He, Himself.

[And this is also the superiority of Eretz Yisrael over other lands, that "Eretz Yisrael is watered by the Holy One, Blessed be He, Himself, and the entire world by a messenger," that in Eretz Yisrael it is openly evident that all the influence of vitality from Above is solely through the Holy One, Blessed be He, whereas in the Diaspora, one might err that there is also a place for a "messenger," and also for the talents and merits of the person, etc.]

From this, it is also understood for our matter: the fact that the key of rain was not entrusted to a messenger (and "rain is also sustenance") means that, in truth, all of a person's sustenance is solely from the Holy One, Blessed be He, in a way that there is no place for anything outside of Him, nor for the "garments" of nature that a person performs so that through them he can receive his sustenance from the Holy One, Blessed be He. And the fact that "a person goes out to his work and his labor until evening" in the business of sustenance is only to fulfill the command of the Holy One, Blessed be He: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do," "Six days you shall work and do all your labor."

Furthermore: not only does the person know that the influence itself comes only from Above—"The blessing of Hashem, it enriches"—and all his actions are nothing but "vessels of reception" for the blessing of Hashem (similar to the vessels of oil of Elisha’s miracle, whose entire purpose was only to contain the miraculous oil), but more than that: the "vessels" themselves have no importance even as "vessels" (and garments) to contain the blessing of Hashem, and he does them only because of the command of the Holy One, Blessed be He. If so, they are completely secondary to the blessing of Hashem, which is a blessing that is entirely above the way of nature.

5. However, this recognition itself can be in two ways:
a) The actions of the person and the garments of nature have no importance at all. Just as in a miraculous conduct it is seen and revealed in practice that the laws of nature have no existence at all—so too, in the exact same way, it is when the influence from the Holy One, Blessed be He, comes through the garments of nature, just like the *Man* that descended from the heavens;
b) Even though the actions of the person and the vessel he makes have no place of their own and he does this only because of the command of Hashem, nevertheless, because of the command of Hashem itself, they have importance, for through them His will is fulfilled.

In other words: His faith is in absolute certainty that everything comes only from the Holy One, Blessed be He, and consequently, he is in complete trust in the Holy One, Blessed be He, that He will give him everything from His full, open, holy, and wide hand. But also regarding this matter—that the Holy One, Blessed be He, commanded that he perform an action in this in nature—he knows that this too is with a specific intent, namely, to know and recognize that nature itself, and the person's action in this, also come from Him, may He be blessed, in addition to the influence itself that comes from the Holy One, Blessed be He.

It can be said that these are the two ways of whether the key of sustenance is counted as a separate key, or if it is included in the key of rain:
To Rabbi Yochanan, "rain (is also) sustenance," because all the garments of nature, as well as the actions of the person in this, have no place at all—and this is what he teaches us: that in relation to the matter of sustenance, all his actions in this are a detail in the influence of the Holy One, Blessed be He, to the person.
And "In the West they say: also sustenance, as it is written: 'You open Your hand, etc.'"—meaning that even the actions of the person in this come from the Holy One, Blessed be He, and it is a separate matter. And this also relates to the person's knowledge and recognition, that the garments of nature and the person's actions are not just something that has no separate existence, but that this itself comes from the Holy One, Blessed be He.

6. According to this, the connection to the disputants is also explained:
Our Sages said: "One who sees Yochanan in a dream, miracles of miracles are done for him" (for a name that has one *nun* indicates a miracle, and a name that has more than one *nun* indicates many miracles). Therefore, Rabbi Yochanan holds that sustenance is included in rain, because from the perspective of his level, "miracles of miracles," he sees in every matter in the world only the miracle within it. And this is the matter of "miracles of miracles"—that the miracle is not only in a thing where it is seen openly that the systems of nature are overturned, but that even in the conduct of nature, from the perspective of Rabbi Yochanan’s level, it is in its essence only a miracle coming from Above.

However, "In the West they say" that the key of rain is a separate key, for "the West" means a specific place in the world, and our Sages said that the *Shechinah* is in the West. This means that even though "the whole earth is full of His glory" and our Sages said there is no place empty of Him, that the entire existence of place is nullified to Him, may He be blessed, nevertheless, "the *Shechinah* is in the West," that this "place" has a special inspiration, to the point that the existence of the place itself is *Elokus*. Therefore, those in the "West" hold that even the garments of nature, "sustenance," are a separate matter that is in the hand of the Holy One, Blessed be He.

7. 18th of Elul—the birthday of the two great luminaries, the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe—falls in most years in the week (or on Shabbos) of *Parshas Tavo*. The essence of these two birthday celebrants corresponds to the two ways of serving Hashem mentioned above: through the Baal Shem Tov in the general *Toras HaChassidus*, and through the Alter Rebbe in the *Toras Chassidus Chabad*.

The innovation revealed by the Baal Shem Tov in the general *Toras HaChassidus* is an additional general vitality in the fulfillment of *Torah* and *mitzvos*. Therefore, one of the matters emphasized in the general *Toras HaChassidus* is the matter of faith: "And the righteous shall live by his faith." This faith is general and in the category of *makif* (encompassing), meaning that even when the faith is in such a way that it is not literally in the category of *makif* (that it does not have an effect on the person—and a thief at the mouth of the tunnel calls to the Merciful One), but rather it activates vitality in all his affairs, and even to actual conduct, all his powers are not a separate matter but a detail in the revelation of faith.

And the Alter Rebbe, in the revelation of *Toras Chassidus Chabad*, innovated (continuing the revelation of the Baal Shem Tov’s general *Toras HaChassidus*) that not only is the point of faith felt also in *Chabad* (intellect), etc., but that this becomes a separate matter as well: that the entire existence of *Chabad* (intellect) in his soul is what grasps *Elokus*, and likewise in the *midos* (emotions) of the heart, that their existence is not just a place for the revelation of the point of faith (a detail in the revelation of faith), but that this is their very existence—the love of Hashem and the fear of Hashem.

And this too is in accordance with the revelation of the unity of Hashem as revealed by the Baal Shem Tov and as continued and revealed by the Alter Rebbe:
Through the Baal Shem Tov, the matter of "There is nothing else besides Him" was revealed—that there is no existence other than Him, may He be blessed. This is also felt in the service of Hashem, that there is no place for his service, but his entire being is a revelation of the point of faith in his soul that exists in every Jew from the side of his soul, which is above the existence of the person.
And through the Alter Rebbe, the matter of the unity of Hashem was revealed even as it is from the perspective of the world, that not only is the existence of the world not in contradiction to His unity, may He be blessed, but that through the world the depth of "Hashem is One" is revealed, that the existence of the world is unified in Him, may He be blessed, as explained at length in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* by the Alter Rebbe.

And so it is also in the service of the person, that not only are all his powers in accordance with the point of faith in the One Hashem, but that this is the entire existence of the intellect within him, that the intellect itself, from the side of its essence, recognizes and feels the unity of Hashem from the perspective of its very existence, for the existence of the intellect itself is not a thing separate from Him, may He be blessed. And so it is with all the powers of his soul.

And this comes specifically through the exertion and service of the person, service by his own power specifically, to understand and grasp the unity of Hashem even in his intellect and even to the intellect in his animal soul, and through contemplation this is drawn also into his *midos*, the love of Hashem and the fear of Hashem, in a way that the love and fear belong to the existence of the *midos* in the heart. And so it is with all the powers of his soul, that it is seen and evident that the true existence of every power in the soul is in its essence *Elokus*.

And through "Your springs shall spread outward" (of the Baal Shem Tov), which is done (primarily) through its continuation in *Chabad* in the soul in *Toras Chassidus Chabad*, and from there to the *midos* and to the heart, and it divides to all the limbs, the Master, this King Moshiach, will come, immediately and truly.

(From a *sicha* of Shabbos Parshas Balak, 5741)


## ר"ה (תשנ"ב)

## 43

### Rosh Hashanah (5752)

1. Rabbeinu HaZaken writes in his Siddur in the "Order of the Tekios": "After the Torah reading one should prepare himself to blow the Shofar and recite this chapter [Psalm 47] seven times."
Simply put, Admur HaZaken is stating two distinct matters here: (a) "prepare himself to blow the Shofar"; (b) "recite this chapter seven times."
[This is especially true given that the sources for these two matters are different. The statement "after the Torah reading one should prepare himself to blow the Shofar" originates in *Pri Etz Chaim* and *Mishnas Chassidim*, where no mention is made of reciting Psalm 47. Conversely, the matter of reciting Psalm 47 originates in the Siddur of the Arizal, yet there (even though the *kavanos* for the Shofar blowing are brought), nothing is found regarding the preparation for the Shofar blowing—"after the Torah reading one should prepare himself to blow the Shofar"].
It requires study: why did Admur HaZaken state "prepare himself to blow the Shofar" in a general way, without specifying the manner of preparation?
Now, in *Pri Etz Chaim* and *Mishnas Chassidim* there, it continues: "(one should prepare himself, etc., to blow the Shofar) to arouse Ze'er Anpin, etc.," and it details the general *kavanah* (according to the secret) of the Shofar blowing. From this, it is understood that the preparation ("prepare himself") pertains to the *kavanah* of the Shofar blowing—that one must prepare himself in such a way that through the Shofar blowing and its *kavanos*, Ze'er Anpin will be aroused, etc.
If the reason Admur HaZaken did not transcribe the *kavanos* of the Shofar blowing in the Siddur is in accordance with his general practice in the Siddur not to transcribe the *kavanos* of the Arizal, because they are not something accessible to every soul —then he should not

## 44

have transcribed the beginning of the language of *Pri Etz Chaim* and *Mishnas Chassidim*, "prepare himself," either. And if he holds that regarding Shofar blowing it is an exception and the *kavanos* of the Shofar blowing are accessible to every soul, he should have transcribed the *kavanos* (in general, at least) explicitly (similar to what we find in the Pesach Haggadah, where he transcribed the *kavanos* for spilling the wine while reciting the plagues, etc.).

2. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his book *Sha'ar HaKollel* (on the Siddur of Admur HaZaken), explains that what Admur HaZaken wrote, "prepare himself to blow the Shofar and recite, etc."—"the preparation is [in this very act] that he recites this Psalm seven times" [meaning that the *vav* in "and recite" is a *vav* of explanation]. For the reason for reciting this Psalm is that through it, one transforms the attribute of *din* into the attribute of *rachamim* (as explained in the Siddur of the Arizal there, and based on the words of the Midrash), and this is the effect of the Shofar blowing, as explained in *Pri Etz Chaim*, that through the Shofar, "the *dinim* and *gevuros* of the name *Elokim* are elevated and sweetened." Thus, it turns out that reciting this Psalm seven times is one of the *kavanos* of the Shofar blowing.
One should add an explanation to this, by first introducing a general matter regarding the Siddur of Admur HaZaken: even though he established the text of the prayers according to the *kavanos* of the Arizal, so that it would be precise according to what emerges from Kabbalah (in addition to it being precise according to grammar and language), he nevertheless did not transcribe the *kavanos* themselves in his Siddur, because it is not something that pertains to every soul, as mentioned above.
Generally, it is implied that the matter of *kavanos* pertains only to select individuals (who know how to direct these *kavanos*). However, it seems more likely to say that the very fact that Admur HaZaken established the text of the prayers (which is a text accessible to every soul) directed according to the *kavanos* of the Arizal is because through the prayer itself in this text (even by those who do not know about the *kavanos*), the *hemshech* and so on, which are in the *kavanos* of the Arizal, are actually effected.
For this very reason, Admur HaZaken instituted a prayer text based on the *kavanos* of the Arizal, so that all of Israel would be connected to the matter of these *kavanos*.
It can be said that this is similar to what Admur HaZaken wrote in his *Hilchos Talmud Torah* regarding the study of the secret part

## 45

of the Torah: "that every soul needs for its rectification to occupy itself with *Pardes*, etc. It must come in reincarnation until it achieves and knows everything possible for its soul to achieve from the knowledge of the Torah, both in the plain meanings of the *halachos* and in the hints, homiletics, and secrets." This means that every soul must occupy itself with achieving the secrets of the Torah. Something similar, and perhaps even more so, applies to the *kavanos* of prayer according to the secret—that they pertain to every soul, except that the majority of the public (who do not know how to actually direct the *kavanos*) are connected only to the "effected" result, that through prayer in this text, the matters are effected. The words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, are well-known : "It is known and received... that those whose minds are not refined enough to direct *kavanos* due to a lack of knowledge, etc., it is sufficient that they direct a general *kavanah*: that their prayer be heard before Him, blessed be He, with all the *kavanos* explained in the books of Kabbalah."
And it is the same regarding the *kavanos* of the Shofar blowing, which pertain to every soul, except that the effect of the matters—for the majority of the public (who do not know how to direct all the *kavanos*)—is through reciting Psalm 47 seven times.

3. But it is difficult to interpret the intention of Admur HaZaken this way, because: (a) The simple reading of the language "prepare, etc., and recite" implies that they are two separate matters. (b) And most importantly: since, according to the above, there is no preparation here other than reciting Psalm 47 seven times—he should have only stated the essential point regarding the action: "recite this chapter seven times." Why did he preface it by transcribing from other sources "prepare himself"?
And even if you say that this language emphasizes that through reciting the Psalm, the matter of the *kavanos* of the Shofar blowing is effected (as above)—what is the practical difference of this emphasis in a Siddur that is accessible to every soul? We do not find in other places in the Siddur that Admur HaZaken hints at how the matters in the *kavanos* are effected; he only established the prayer text in accordance with them.
It is more reasonable to say that when Admur HaZaken wrote the general language "prepare himself," he did not intend the preparation pertaining to the *kavanos* of the Shofar blowing found in *Pri Etz Chaim* and *Mishnas Chassidim* (which he did not transcribe in his Siddur), but rather, as the language simply reads, that the *baal tokeia* must prepare himself for the Shofar blowing, as is also brought in *Mateh Efraim* regarding the custom to perform a "great preparation" for the Shofar blowing. Admur HaZaken did not specify any particular preparation because it is not something accessible to every soul, as there are many ways in which one can arouse oneself and prepare for the Shofar blowing (as several of them are brought in *Mateh Efraim* there), and each individual must prepare himself for the Shofar blowing according to his own capacity.

4. However, this still does not answer the question: why only here, regarding the *mitzvah* of Shofar blowing, did Admur HaZaken write that one must prepare himself to fulfill the *mitzvah*? After all, the proper fulfillment of every *mitzvah* is when it is done with the appropriate *kavanah* (for a *mitzvah* without *kavanah* is like a body without a soul), yet we do not find that Admur HaZaken wrote in his Siddur regarding other *mitzvos* brought in his Siddur (such as *tzitzis*, *tefillin*, *netilas lulav*, and others) that a person must prepare himself before performing the *mitzvah*.

## 46

On the face of it, this can be explained according to what the Rambam writes : "Even though the blowing of the Shofar on Rosh Hashanah is a decree of the Torah, there is a hint in it, namely: 'Awaken, you sleepers, from your slumber, etc., and search your deeds and return in repentance, etc.'" Seemingly, one must be precise: why did the Rambam bring these words of *aggadah* in the *Yad*, which is a book of *halacha*? It implies, seemingly, that this "hint" relates to the *halacha*, that the blowing of the Shofar is not only a *mitzvah* of action (hearing the sound of the Shofar) but also a *mitzvah* of the heart, that the sound of the Shofar must awaken a person to repentance, and without this, something is lacking in the very fulfillment of the *mitzvah* [similar (though not exactly) to the well-known words of the *Bach* regarding *tzitzis*, *tefillin*, and *sukkah*, that the fulfillment of these *mitzvos* also depends on their *kavanah*]. For this reason, Admur HaZaken wrote that one must prepare himself for the Shofar blowing, because without this, something is lacking in the very fulfillment of the *mitzvah*.
But it is forced to interpret it this way, because we do not find in the books of the *poskim* that without *kavanah* and the arousal of repentance, something is lacking in the fulfillment of the *mitzvah* of Shofar blowing. Also, regarding the Rambam, it is difficult to interpret it this way, for if so, he should have brought this matter in *Hilchos Shofar*. The fact that he brought it only in *Hilchos Teshuvah* and not in *Hilchos Shofar* proves that this "hint" is not part of the fulfillment of the *mitzvah* of Shofar.

5. It is possible to provide the explanation for this by first introducing a general wonder regarding the Siddur of Admur HaZaken: in the books of Kabbalah, it is stated that before every *mitzvah*, one must say "For the sake of the unification of the Holy One, blessed be He, and His *Shechinah*", and in many *Siddurim*, this text is brought before the fulfillment of several *mitzvos*. We find a wondrous thing in the Siddur of Admur HaZaken: he did not establish that one should say "For the sake of the unification" before fulfilling a *mitzvah* (as we find in the *mitzvos* brought in his Siddur), but on the other hand, he did establish that it be said every day in the prayer before *Baruch She'amar*.
It is explained regarding this that "we say 'For the sake of the unification' before prayer, and through this, we fulfill it for the entire day regarding the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, etc.".
But it still requires explanation: if this is a practice that pertains to every person, why did he not establish that it be said before performing every *mitzvah*? And if it is not something accessible to every soul, why did he establish it before *Baruch She'amar* ?
It can be said, according to what we explained above (Section 2), that in essence, Admur HaZaken holds that the matter of *kavanos* (also) according to the secret pertains to every soul, but this is only regarding the "effected" result—that every soul is given the power to effect the matters and the *hemshech* detailed

## 47

in the *kavanos* of the *mitzvos*, even though the act of the *kavanos* is not something accessible to every soul.
According to this, it seems possible to say further that Admur HaZaken holds that a person must say "For the sake of the unification" at least once every day, in order to effect the "unification of the Holy One, blessed be He, and His *Shechinah*" in the fulfillment of every single *mitzvah* throughout the entire day. For even though it is not something accessible to every soul to direct "For the sake of the unification, etc." during the fulfillment of every single *mitzvah* throughout the entire day, nevertheless, it is within the power of each and every person to direct this (at least each according to his own capacity) during the time of prayer. And this recitation and *kavanah* at the beginning of the day is a continuous action for all things done during this day, as mentioned above. Therefore, he established that it be said in the morning prayer, and in this very matter, at the beginning of the prayer, before *Baruch She'amar*.

6. According to this premise, one can also explain the position of Admur HaZaken regarding the *kavanos* for the Shofar blowing:
What Admur HaZaken wrote, that one must prepare himself for the Shofar blowing and that hearing the sound of the Shofar alone is not sufficient, is understood because in the Siddur of Admur HaZaken, which was established according to the secret, the matter of preparation and *kavanah* in the *mitzvos* is of the utmost importance. However, since this is a Siddur accessible to every soul, therefore, in this matter as well, Admur HaZaken adopted a path accessible to every soul, in that he did not obligate the matter of preparation before every single *mitzvah*, but only before the Shofar blowing.
For just as it is regarding every single day, that Admur HaZaken established that one should say "For the sake of the unification" once at the beginning of the day, which effects the entire day, as mentioned above, something similar is the case regarding the entirety of the year. In this general *mitzvah* of Shofar blowing at the beginning of the year, the matter of preparation is required, and through this, it is also drawn down for the entire year.
For it is explained in many places that the Shofar blowing is a general *mitzvah* that pertains to a person's service throughout the entire year. Rosh Hashanah is called "Head" (and not the beginning of the year) because it is like the head that leads the entire body, and thus, a person's service during the time of Rosh Hashanah influences his service throughout the entire year. And in this very matter, "the *mitzvah* of the day is with the Shofar", which is the primary *mitzvah* (and service) of Rosh Hashanah. Therefore, even though the matter of *kavanah* and preparation in every *mitzvah* is not something accessible to every soul, nevertheless, regarding the Shofar blowing, which is in the category of a "head" for the entire year, the preparation must be manifest among all of Israel.
According to this, one can explain with greater depth the language of Admur HaZaken, "prepare himself to blow the Shofar," without specifying what the preparation is—that this is not only because it depends on each individual according to his capacity (as in Section 3), but because it is in accordance with the content of the service of the Shofar blowing, which is the first service as a "head" for a person's service throughout the entire year. The content of this "beginning" is the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, a general acceptance of the yoke. This means that the service of the day is not just making good resolutions to improve oneself in specific matters

## 48

of Torah, service, and acts of kindness, but it is a general surrender to Hashem from the depths of the soul.
And this is what Admur HaZaken meant by "prepare himself to blow the Shofar," without writing any specific matter, because this is the entire content of the Shofar blowing: a general preparation for the service of Hashem throughout the entire year that transcends details.
(From a *sicha* of *Shabbos Parshas Ha'azinu* 5731)


## דף השער

## 119

### Title Page

**Additions**
**Likkutei Sichos**
**Explanations on Iggeres HaTeshuvah**
a) Explanations in Likutei Levi Yitzchak, Chapters 1–4
b) Explanations in Iggeres HaTeshuvah, Chapters 1–4


## ביאורים לאגה"ת (א)

## 121

### Explanations to Iggeres HaTeshuvah (1)

**Additions**
**Iggeres HaTeshuvah**
1. At the beginning of Chapter 3 of Iggeres HaTeshuvah, the Alter Rebbe cites the opinion that "one who has committed a certain sin many times... must fast the number of fasts prescribed for that sin as many times as the number of times he sinned." He provides an example: "For instance, one who has spilled seed in vain, for whom the number of fasts specified in the *Tikkunei Teshuvah* of the Arizal is 84 fasts—if he sinned in this way ten or twenty times, for example, he must fast 84 fasts ten or twenty times, and so on forever."

In the notes of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, it is explained: "He chose the example of 'ten or twenty'... because in the case of spilling seed... the blemish is in the *moach* (as stated later in Chapter 9), which is *Chochma*, and *Chochma* is the letter *yud* of the Name *Havayah* (as stated later in Chapter 4)... This is 'ten,' meaning the *yud*. But the *yud* in its fullness (*milui*), *yud-vav-dalet*, is twenty; this is 'or twenty'."

This requires clarification: The substance of the Alter Rebbe’s statement here (that according to this opinion, "one must fast... as many times as the number of times he sinned") applies to every sin, and the sin of "spilling seed in vain" was brought here only as an example ("for instance, one who has spilled..."). If so, what is the practical difference in hinting here at the place that is blemished (the *moach* of *Chochma*) by this specific sin?

Furthermore: The precision of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the Alter Rebbe "chose the example of 'ten or twenty'" is not because he *had* to choose a different number [in which case one could argue, albeit with difficulty, that since he had to choose *some* number as an example, he chose the one that hints at the blemish of this sin]. Rather, the precision is: Why bring an example for the number of times at all? What would have been missing if the Alter Rebbe had simply stated, "One must fast 84 [fasts] for each time," without bringing a specific number as an example?

Since this is the case, it is puzzling: Why does the Alter Rebbe add an example for the number of times one has sinned (which is in itself unnecessary) solely to hint at the place of the blemish of the sin he brought as an example?

2. Regarding the aforementioned precision [why the Alter Rebbe brought an example for the number of times one sinned ("ten or twenty")]—there is a more general precision in the Alter Rebbe’s words here (which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, did not address): Why was it necessary to bring an example from a specific sin at all? His words, "one who has committed a certain sin many times... [must fast] the number of fasts for that sin... as the number of times he sinned," are clear even without an example from a specific sin. Why did he add, "for instance, one who has spilled seed in vain, etc."?

## 122

One must also understand the Alter Rebbe’s addition—after writing, "And if he sinned in this way ten or twenty times, for example, he must fast 84 fasts ten or twenty times"—the words "and so on forever" (meaning that if he sinned more than twenty times, he must fast 84 fasts for each time). Seemingly, what does this teach us? Why would it enter our minds that the rule "he must fast... as the number of times he sinned" applies only up to twenty times, such that it is necessary to explicitly negate this notion with the addition "and so on forever"??

3. In the notes of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, he explains (in parentheses) another precision in Iggeres HaTeshuvah here:
Later in the chapter, the Alter Rebbe writes: "Every soul-possessor... should be stringent upon himself to complete at least once in his lifetime the number of fasts for every one of the severe sins for which one is liable to death, at least, and even if only by the hand of Heaven, such as for spilling seed in vain, 84 fasts once in his lifetime. And he may defer them... and fast about ten fasts, for example, in one winter." My father-in-law, the Rebbe, explains that "the reason he chose [also here]... 'about ten fasts' is because 'about ten is also *yud*'."

Here, too, one must be precise regarding the Alter Rebbe’s words (and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, did not address this): Why was it necessary to bring an example ("such as for spilling seed in vain, etc.")?
Also, one must understand: Since the letter *yud* relates not only to the number ten but also to the number twenty, as mentioned above—what is the reason (in the inner dimension of the matters) that regarding "and he shall fast... in one winter," he brings only the number ten and not the number twenty?

4. It has already been explained several times regarding the notes of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on the *Zohar* and *Tanya*, etc., that for several reasons (including the limitation of paper and ink), they were written with extreme brevity. When one studies them with the proper depth, one sees that in addition to the precisions he explains explicitly in these notes, one can find in them a resolution to several other questions that arise in the matter (and sometimes even questions in other places).
Furthermore: Even though in most of the notes he dwells (openly) only on linguistic precisions and the like, after proper study, one sees that in many of them, the general content of the matter he is discussing is also explained and clarified.
This is also the case here: even though he openly explains only the precision of why the Alter Rebbe chose the example of "ten or twenty" (and "about ten fasts"), this note resolves several other precisions, including the aforementioned precisions (sections 2-3).
Moreover, this note also explains the general content of the Alter Rebbe’s words here, both the reason that (according to one opinion) "one must fast the number of fasts for that sin... as the number of times he sinned," and the reason that "every soul-possessor... should be stringent upon himself to complete at least once, etc.," as will be explained below.

## 123

5. The explanation for all of the above:
In the blemish caused by a sin—and consequently also in the rectification of the blemish (through *teshuvah*)—there are, in general, three aspects:
a) Since by every sin one transgresses the command of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He (which is the general point and the common denominator of all transgressions)—by every transgression (including the neglect of a positive commandment), a person casts off the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven and becomes a *rasha*.
The rectification for this is through "the sinner abandoning his sin... and resolving in his heart not to do it again" [in the words of the Alter Rebbe: "that he resolve in his heart with a whole heart never to return to folly to rebel against His Kingdom, may He be blessed, and never again transgress the command of the King, Heaven forbid"]. Through this resolution and acceptance for the future (which is the essence of *teshuvah*), the title of *rasha* is removed from him (immediately). This can happen even in a single moment, as per the ruling of the *Gemara* and the *Poskim*, that through a thought of *teshuvah*, one is transformed from a complete *rasha* to a complete *tzaddik*.
b) Since the integrity and perfection of the limbs of the soul depend on the *mitzvos*—by neglecting a positive commandment or transgressing a negative commandment, a blemish and deficiency is created in the specific limb associated with that specific *mitzvah*.
In order to rectify the specific blemish, a person must perform the *tikkunei teshuvah* associated with this specific transgression, including the number of fasts prescribed for this transgression.
c) Since a corruption in a specific limb also causes (a semblance of) corruption in all of a person's limbs, it follows that by every transgression, a blemish is created in all the powers and limbs (all the more so, given that we find that every action also impacts the entirety of the world outside of the person).

## 124

Therefore, "the ways of *teshuvah*" are not only that a person "distances himself from the thing he sinned in," but also that he "changes all his deeds for the better and to a straight path."
6. The Torah is "stated in generalities and particulars." From this, it is understood that in each of the three aspects above (section 5), there are, in detail, (a semblance of) all three aspects.
Regarding our subject—the number of fasts prescribed for each specific transgression, which is connected to the specific blemish caused by this sin (the second aspect above)—this very blemish contains a semblance of the three aspects mentioned above.
The explanation:
Since all the limbs of the body are included in one another, it follows that in every limb there are three aspects: 1) Its own essence. 2) The other limbs as they are included within it. 3) As this limb is included in the other limbs.
From this, it is understood that the blemish in this specific limb (caused by a specific transgression) is in all three of these aspects.
7. It can be said that regarding the blemish in the essence of the limb, immediately upon the act of transgression the first time, the (essence of the) limb is completely blemished, in such a way that subsequently, no further blemish is added to this [in a primary sense, at least] even if he fails in this sin again.
The blemish in the particulars of the limb (i.e., in the "limbs" included within it, etc.) is completed only upon committing the sin for the third time, as the Alter Rebbe brings from the *Zohar*: "The third time, that stain spreads from this side to that side," meaning that the third time, the stain penetrates all the particulars of the limb (associated with this sin) completely.
Whereas regarding the blemish caused in the other limbs of the body (i.e., in this limb as it is included in the other limbs), it is reasonable to say that every time he commits this sin, the blemish increases. For since he did not transgress the sins associated with those limbs, it is not possible for this blemish to spread through them "from this side to that side."
This is the explanation for the three opinions (brought by the Alter Rebbe in this chapter) regarding "one who has committed a certain sin many times"—how many times one must fast the number of fasts for that sin (and both these and those are the words of the Living G-d): 1) According to the number of times he sinned, 2) It is sufficient to fast the number of fasts once, 3) The "accepted decision... is to fast three times the number of fasts for this sin":
To rectify the blemish in the essence of the limb—the number of fasts once is sufficient (corresponding to the one time by which the essence of the limb was blemished); to rectify the blemish in the other limbs—one must fast for each and every time; and to rectify the blemish in the limbs as they are included in this limb—one must fast three times.
It can be said that for this reason, even though the Alter Rebbe adopted the "accepted decision... to fast three times the number of fasts for this sin," he nevertheless ruled that one must be more stringent the first time one fasts the "number of fasts" than in the second and third times [in which "he shall fast another four times... only until after midday... and two half-days are considered for him as one day," unlike the first time, when he must fast full fasts]—because the blemish in the essence of the limb (the rectification of which is through the number of fasts once) is a more severe blemish than the blemish in the limbs included within it (the rectification of which is by fasting two more times).
8. It can be said that this is one of the reasons why the Alter Rebbe adds the example [when bringing the first opinion "that one must fast... as the number of times he sinned"] "for instance, one who has spilled seed in vain, etc.":
Regarding *shichvat zera*, the Rambam wrote: "Whoever emits it, the body is destroyed, its strength is destroyed, and his life is lost." From this, it is understood that in the sin of spilling seed in vain, it is more openly apparent how (a) the sin also acts upon all the other limbs of the body, (b) each time the blemish increases.
Therefore, the Alter Rebbe adds "for instance, one who has spilled seed in vain, etc."—because in this example, the reason for this opinion (regarding all sins) is explained, that one must fast the number of fasts for each and every time he sinned.
9. In the Rambam there, before his aforementioned words, "And whoever emits it, the body is destroyed, etc., and his life is lost," he wrote: "*Shichvat zera* is the strength of the body and its life, etc." This means that the fact that *shichvat zera* acts upon the entire body is a result and consequence of it being "the strength of the body."
It can be said that the fact that "*shichvat zera* is the strength of the body" (which is that it includes within itself the strength of the entire body) is not its essence, but only an additional aspect of it, and its essence is a drop (a point) that is above definition.
Furthermore: The point of the drop of seed is connected with the point of the soul.
And this fact, that its essence is a point (a drop) connected with the point of the soul, is the reason that it also includes the strength of the body.
10. From this, it is understood regarding the sin of spilling seed in vain, that the severity of the blemish in this sin is in all three of the aforementioned aspects (section 6):
Because the drop of seed is (includes) "the strength of the body" and acts upon the entire body—the blemish caused by this sin in all the other limbs (both as they are included in this limb and as they are in their own place) is more severe than other sins;
And because of its essence (a drop), the blemish caused by this sin in the essence of the limb is also more severe than other sins—since the sin blemishes (not only the essence of a specific limb, but) the essence of a matter connected with the point of the soul.
11. Based on this, one can also explain the reason the Alter Rebbe brings the example of spilling seed in vain three times in this chapter: a) Regarding the opinion "that one must fast... as the number of times he sinned," he adds "for instance, one who has spilled seed in vain, etc."; regarding the "accepted decision... to fast three times," he adds "meaning 252 fasts for spilling seed in vain"; and when writing that "every soul-possessor... should be stringent upon himself to complete at least once, etc.," he adds "such as for spilling seed in vain, 84 fasts once, etc.":
The reason "one must fast... as the number of times he sinned" is because of the blemish caused by this sin in the other limbs as they are in their own place; the reason "to fast three times" is to rectify the blemish in the limbs as they are included in this limb (associated with this sin); and the reason "to complete at least once" the number of fasts as a full fast (and not "two half-days") is because of the severity of the blemish caused in the essence of the limb (as explained at length in section 7)—
And these three aspects are explained by the example of spilling seed in vain, since these three aspects are more emphasized in this sin.
12. Based on all the above, the reason will be understood why, when bringing this example regarding the opinion "that one must fast... as the number of times he sinned," he did not write (simply) "one must fast 84 for each time" (or similar language), but specifies "ten or twenty, etc., and so on forever":
Through fasting "many times as the number of times he sinned," one rectifies all three aspects of the blemish: through the first fast, one rectifies the blemish in the essence of the limb; through fasting two more times, one also rectifies the blemish in the limbs included within it; and through the rest of the fasts (after the first three times), one also rectifies the blemish in the limbs as they are in their own place.
Therefore, the Alter Rebbe specifies the three modes: "ten," "twenty," and "forever"—because these three modes emphasize the three aspects mentioned above, as follows.
13. It is explained in *Chassidus* regarding the *milui* (fullness) of letters, that the *milui* of every letter is only "in order to explain it to another." As the example is brought for this from the letter *yud*, that in thought (and also in writing), one can think (and also write) the letter *yud* as it is in itself; whereas when one expresses the letter *yud* in speech to another, one must also add its *milui*, the letters *vav-dalet*.
Nevertheless, the *milui* (*vav-dalet*) is also included in the letter *yud* itself, but even as it is included in the letter itself, since it is only "in order to explain it to another," it is "not considered of the category of essence, but only something additional to the essence."
Based on this, it is understood how the three modes—"ten," "twenty," and "forever"—relate to the three aforementioned aspects: "ten," which is the number of the letter *yud* itself [which is "like the image of a drop"]—is connected with the blemish (and its rectification) in the *moach* itself; "twenty," the number of the letter *yud* in its *milui*—with the blemish (and its rectification) in the limbs of the body as they are included in the *moach*; and "forever," the times more than twenty—with the blemish (and its rectification) in the body (*olam katan*).
Based on this, the reason is also understood why regarding "and he shall fast... in one winter," the Alter Rebbe brings only the number ten, and not twenty: "and he shall fast... in one winter" refers to the fasts of "84 fasts once," and therefore it relates only to the number ten.
(From a *sicha* of *Shabbos Parshas Eikev* 5730)


## אגרת התשובה ב

## 128

### Igeres HaTeshuvah II

A. At the beginning of chapter 4 of *Igeres HaTeshuvah*, the Alter Rebbe writes: "However, all of the above [i.e., the details regarding the fasts of *teshuvah*, explained in *Igeres HaTeshuvah*, chapters 2-3] is for the completion of the atonement, etc., after the *teshuvah*, etc. However, the beginning of the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* and its essence, etc. [which is the matter of *teshuvah* itself], it is necessary to explain well, with an expanded explanation, by prefacing what is written in the *Zohar HaKadosh* in explanation of the word *teshuvah* according to the secret: *tashuv hei*—the lower *hei* is the lower *teshuvah*, the higher *hei* is the higher *teshuvah*."

In the notes of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, here, he explains that the two expressions, "to explain well" and "with an expanded explanation," correspond to the two levels of *teshuvah* mentioned subsequently: *tashuv hei* (lower) and *tashuv hei* (higher): "The lower *hei* is *Malchus*, and regarding it is 'explain well' (*ba'er heitev*)—*ba'er* is *Malchus*, *heitev* is the *Yesod* of *Ze'er Anpin*. And this is the lower *teshuvah*, [explaining] the lower *hei* of *Malchus* [and this is the lower *teshuvah* itself, which is connected with *Malchus*, the *hei*], *heitev* is the master of the lower *teshuvah* [connected with] *Yesod* [vav], which is the master of *Malchus*. 'With an expanded explanation' corresponds to the higher *teshuvah* of *Binah*, because *Binah* is the aspect of 'wide spaces' (*rechovos*)."

This requires clarification: In the higher *teshuvah* as well, there are two details—*teshuvah* (itself) and the "master of *teshuvah*" : the higher *teshuvah* itself is in *Binah* (the higher *hei*), and the "master of the higher *teshuvah*" is in *Chochma* (the *yud*). According to this, it is not understood: What is the reason for the distinction, that when hinting at the lower *teshuvah*, the Alter Rebbe used language that hints at both aspects—the lower *teshuvah* itself (*Malchus*) and the master of the lower *teshuvah* (*Yesod* of *Ze'er Anpin*), whereas when hinting at the higher *teshuvah*, he says "with an expanded explanation," which hints only at the higher *teshuvah* (Binah) itself, and not at the aspect of the "master of the higher *teshuvah*" (*Chochma*) ?

Also, one must understand:
The words "to explain well with an expanded explanation" refer (simply) to "what is written in the *Zohar HaKadosh* in explanation of the word *teshuvah* according to the secret, etc."—whereas from the Alter Rebbe's language, "by prefacing what is written in the *Zohar HaKadosh*, etc.," it is implied that through the preface "what is written in the *Zohar HaKadosh*, etc.," he comes to explain (in "to explain well with an expanded explanation") a different matter.

B. In addition to the aforementioned precision, one must understand the general matter explained here, that in order to understand "the beginning of the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* and its essence, etc.—it is necessary to explain, etc., by prefacing what is written in the *Zohar HaKadosh* in explanation of the word *teshuvah* according to the secret"—for seemingly:

The explanation of "the word *teshuvah* according to the secret"—"*tashuv hei*"—emphasizes only what is accomplished by *teshuvah* (that through sin one brings down the lower *hei* (which is the *Shechinah*) into exile, and through "proper *teshuvah*"—"*tashuv* the lower *hei* from the state of exile"), but it adds no explanation or addition (at least not an essential one) to the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* itself (which the person is obligated in), regarding what the Alter Rebbe already wrote above that "the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah*... is the abandonment of the sin, etc., that he should resolve in his heart with a whole heart, etc."

However, from the Alter Rebbe's language, "the beginning of the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* and its essence, etc., it is necessary to explain, etc., the word *teshuvah* according to the secret," it is implied that the preface of the explanation of the word *teshuvah* according to the secret is necessary (also) for the sake of explaining the "*mitzvah* of *teshuvah*" (i.e., the command that the person must fulfill)—and furthermore, that this preface is necessary even for the explanation of "the beginning of the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* and its essence."

C. Furthermore:
The Alter Rebbe brings from the "*Zohar HaKadosh*" not only "the explanation of the word *teshuvah* according to the secret, *tashuv hei*," but also that there are two levels in this, lower *teshuvah* and higher *teshuvah*, from which it is understood that for the sake of explaining "the beginning of the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* and its essence," the preface of the explanation in the level of higher *teshuvah* is also required.

This requires clarification: The distinction between the two levels of lower *teshuvah* and higher *teshuvah* is explained later in *Igeres HaTeshuvah*, that lower *teshuvah* is what a person returns to his previous standing and state as it was before the sin—"to wash and cleanse their souls from the filthy garments," and higher *teshuvah* (which comes after lower *teshuvah*) is the returning of the soul "to its source, etc., as it was unified with Him, may He be blessed, in the ultimate unity before He breathed it into the spirit of His mouth, may He be blessed, to descend below and be clothed in the body of man."

And it is not understood: How is it possible to say (as above, beginning of section A), that the matters that come "for the completion of the atonement and the cleansing of the soul" (so that he should be "acceptable and beloved, etc., as before the sin") are "after the *teshuvah*," and are not included in the "*mitzvah* of *teshuvah*"; and (the explanation of) the matter of higher *teshuvah* [returning the soul to its source, etc., as it was, etc., before He breathed, etc., a matter that must also be in one who has never sinned in his life, and seemingly does not relate at all to the correction of the sin] relates to the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah*, and even to "the beginning of the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* and its essence"?

D. The explanation of all the above will be understood by prefacing what is explained in many places that lower *teshuvah* is connected with the *avodah* of "turn from evil and do good"—the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, and higher *teshuvah*—with the engagement in Torah [as is also brought later in *Igeres HaTeshuvah* from "R.M. in *Parshas Naso*" that "higher *teshuvah* is that he should engage in Torah, etc."].

And it can be said (one of the explanations) regarding this:
In the *avodah* of fulfilling *mitzvos*, the matter of *bitul* and the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven is expressed, that the person is prepared to obey all the commands of the *Ribono shel Olam*, even when it is connected with difficulties—like a servant who obeys the command of the master, without taking into account any calculations.

Not so the *bitul* in "engagement in Torah," which is that "the word of Hashem, this is *Halacha*, it is... that speaks from within his throat." Therefore they said, "Who are the kings? The Rabbis", because from the perspective of the aforementioned *bitul* in engagement in Torah, he is not only "like a servant who fulfills the commands of the King," but his very existence is the "King".

And it can be said that this *bitul* (in engagement in Torah) is from the root of the soul as it was "before He breathed, etc.": From the perspective of the aspect of the soul as it descended below, indeed (in the language of the *Tanya*) "the soul of man, even if he is a completely righteous person, etc., is not nullified in existence entirely, etc., to be one and unified in a complete unity, etc."; not so the aforementioned *bitul* and unity in engagement in Torah, which comes from the illumination of the aspect of the soul as it is "before He breathed," when it was "unified with Him, may He be blessed, in the ultimate unity."

And according to this, the connection of lower *teshuvah* to the fulfillment of *mitzvos* ("turn from evil and do good") and higher *teshuvah* to engagement in Torah is understood:

The *bitul* that is from the perspective of the aspect of the soul as it is already after the "He breathed"—and especially after its descent below into this world and its clothing in a body—is only like the *bitul* of a servant to a king (and the like), meaning, as "existence" is in a state of *bitul* relative to the *Ribono shel Olam*;

And this is what lower *teshuvah* relates primarily to the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, that the *bitul* in this *avodah* is "like a servant who fulfills the commands of the King," because the matter of lower *teshuvah* is (primarily) the return to his previous standing and state as it was before the sin ("to wash and cleanse their souls from the filthy garments, etc."), when he was also an "existence," as mentioned.

Not so higher *teshuvah*, whose matter is the returning of the soul to its source "as it was unified with Him, may He be blessed, in the ultimate unity before He breathed, etc.", for this level in *teshuvah* is connected with engagement in Torah, that "the word of Hashem... is... that speaks from within his throat."

E. And behold, in each of the two aforementioned aspects (lower *teshuvah* and higher *teshuvah*) themselves, there are two aspects of *teshuvah*, and they are the two levels of "*teshuvah*" and "master of *teshuvah*," which exist both in lower *teshuvah* and in higher *teshuvah* (as mentioned in section A).

The explanation of the matter:
Regarding the two aspects that are in lower *teshuvah*, it is explained in *Chassidus* that the lower level within it ("*teshuvah*" itself) is connected with the *avodah* of "turn from evil," and that is what a person accomplishes in himself so that he will not be connected to doing anything that is the opposite of the will of Hashem; and the higher level in lower *teshuvah* (the aspect of "master of lower *teshuvah*") is connected with the *avodah* of "do good," and it is "to weary himself in Torah and *tefillah*" more than his nature and habit—and it is the aspect of the "servant of Hashem" who "repeats his chapter one hundred and one times," more than his habit.

And from this it is understood that the two aspects of "*teshuvah*" and "master of *teshuvah*" (that are in lower *teshuvah*) are like the level of lower *teshuvah* and higher *teshuvah*:
In the *avodah* of "turn from evil," the worker remains in his existence, and only that the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven that he accepted upon himself prevents him from transgressing the will of the Almighty. And therefore it relates to lower *teshuvah* (in lower *teshuvah* itself);

Not so the *avodah* of "do good," to weary himself in Torah, etc., more than his habit through the breaking of his nature, for in this the person "exits" (to a certain extent) from his existence, and therefore it relates to higher *teshuvah*.

But nevertheless, even the *avodah* of "do good" (which is above "turn from evil") is only a level in lower *teshuvah* [and only that in lower *teshuvah* itself it is the aspect of higher *teshuvah* within it], because: (a) even in the *avodah* of "do good" he did not exit entirely from his existence, but only overcame his nature through a battle. (b) More than this: even changing his habit is an action of the person (not like in engagement in Torah where the word of Hashem is the one "speaking from within his throat").

F. And behold, even the *avodah* of engagement in Torah that is connected with higher *teshuvah* as mentioned, is only the level of "*teshuvah*" itself (in higher *teshuvah*), whereas the level of "master of higher *teshuvah*" is the *avodah* of "sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you". And according to the above (section E) that "*teshuvah*" and "master of *teshuvah*" are a parallel to lower *teshuvah* and higher *teshuvah*, it is understood that in higher *teshuvah* itself, engagement in Torah is the aspect of lower *teshuvah* within it, and "sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you"—the aspect of higher *teshuvah* within it.

The explanation of the matter:
Regarding the verse "And you shall be to Me a treasure, etc.," it is stated in the *Mechilta*: "'And you shall be to Me'—that you should be acquired by Me and engage in Torah and not be engaged in other things," and that is, that "engaging in Torah" alone is not sufficient to reach the true matter of "acquired by Me," but the condition is also required that "you shall not be engaged in other things," which is the *avodah* of "sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you."

For this, that a person engages in Torah, even when his engagement in Torah is in a manner that "the word of Hashem, etc., is... that speaks from within his throat," is not proof that he is "acquired" in his entire existence to Hashem—for it is possible that his *bitul* in engagement in Torah is from the fact that the Torah has permeated him to such an extent that his existence has been nullified; but this is not proof that he is from his own side nullified in existence to *Elokus*.

Not so in the *avodah* of "sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you," meaning that he sanctifies himself and separates from his private needs ("other things"), even though they are "permitted to you"—it is emphasized that he is "nullifying and removing himself and his will to be nullified to Him, may He be blessed", that he has no existence for himself, and his entire existence is "acquired by Me."

According to this, it is understood that the true matter of higher *teshuvah* is expressed in the *avodah* of "sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you," not so the *bitul* of engagement in Torah, which is only the aspect of lower *teshuvah* in higher *teshuvah*:
The matter of higher *teshuvah* is "to cleave to Him, may He be blessed, in a wondrous unity, as it was unified with Him, may He be blessed, in the ultimate unity before He breathed, etc.," and it is not appropriate to say that then ("before He breathed") the soul had any existence for itself. And since the *bitul* of engagement in Torah does not negate (entirely) the existence of the person, as mentioned, therefore it is only the aspect of lower *teshuvah* in higher *teshuvah*; not so the *avodah* of "sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you," in which it is emphasized that the entire existence of the person is acquired to Hashem, it is a higher level and it is the true matter of higher *teshuvah*.

G. According to this, it is also understood the reason that the *avodah* of "sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you" is from the perspective of the aspect of *Chochma* in the soul, the aspect of *yud* (a point), as mentioned (section A) that "master of higher *teshuvah*" is the aspect of *yud*—because through this *avodah* is revealed the essence of the point of connection (of Israel with the *Kudsha Brich Hu*) which is *yud*, a point, which is above form:

The connection (of Israel with the *Kudsha Brich Hu*) in the three *avodos* of "turn from evil," "do good," and the *bitul* of engagement in Torah, comes in some form. For since in them the person has not yet exited from his existence entirely, and the *avodah* is to connect his existence with the *Ribono shel Olam*, therefore, the manner of connection is formed according to the form of the powers of the person that are in them and through them this connection is accomplished; and therefore these three *avodos* relate to the three letters *hei*, *vav*, *hei* (of the name *Havayah*), which have a form.

Not so the *avodah* of "sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you," whose matter is that "he nullifies and removes himself and his will" and it reveals the essence of the point of connection that is above the category and form of the powers of the person—it is hinted at in the letter *yud*, a point.

H. Just as the four letters of the name *Havayah* begin with the point of the letter *yud*, and this point is drawn afterwards into the form of the first letter *hei*, and afterwards into the form of the letter *vav*, and up to the form of the last *hei* —so it is also regarding the four aforementioned *avodos*, which are not separate *avodos* and matters (in their essence), but they are one continuation:

Their beginning and their essence is—the point of the connection of Israel with the *Ribono shel Olam* that is above form (which comes to expression in the negation of his existence—"nullifies and removes himself and his will, etc.," sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you), and this point of connection is drawn afterwards into the aspect of form in engagement in Torah, in "do good," up to "turn from evil."

And therefore, when there is a lack in the *bitul* of the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven in the *avodah* of "turn from evil," this harms not only the lower *hei*, but also the three letters that preceded it. For if the point of *bitul* itself (*yud*) were illuminating for him, or at least as it is in the form of "engagement in Torah" and "do good" (the first *hei* and the letter *vav*), the *bitul* of the acceptance of the yoke would not be lacking for him.

And this is also the reason that when a person fails in a sin, there must be for him also higher *teshuvah*, because specifically then his *teshuvah* is a "complete *teshuvah*".

I. Furthermore:
Not only for the sake of the completeness of *teshuvah* are they in need of the *avodah* of higher *teshuvah* that comes after lower *teshuvah*, but furthermore, that lower *teshuvah* itself must be in a manner that there will be felt in it (in practice, at least) the movement of higher *teshuvah*.

That is to say, that the acceptance for the future "that he should not return again to folly to rebel against His Kingdom, may He be blessed, and he will not transgress again the command of the King, *chas v'shalom*" must be in a manner that there will be felt in it not only the *bitul* of the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven [like a servant who is prepared to obey the command of the master, even though his existence is not the existence of the master], but also that his *bitul* is caused and a result of this, that he is unified (from the perspective of the root of his soul) with the *Ribono shel Olam* in the ultimate unity.

*Yud*. And it can be said that this is also the explanation (in *avodah*) in this, that the matter of lower *teshuvah* is (not only "*tashuv* the lower *hei* from the state of exile", but also) "*tashuv* the lower *hei* to its place to be unified in *yud-hei-vav*" :

The matter of the lower *hei* by itself (in the *avodah* of man) is the *bitul* of the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven from the perspective of the aspect of the soul clothed in the body ; whereas the matter of "*tashuv* the lower *hei* to its place to be unified in *yud-hei-vav*" is that the *bitul* of the acceptance of the yoke (the lower *hei*) should be in a manner that there will be felt in it that it is connected and unified with the "ultimate unity" that is from the perspective of the essence of the soul, the letters *yud-hei-vav*.

K. According to all the above, it will be understood how the explanation of the word *teshuvah* according to the secret (*tashuv hei*) adds understanding to the "*mitzvah* of *teshuvah*" (that is upon the person):

Through the length of the explanation of how the lower *hei* is not a matter by itself but is a continuation from the three preceding letters, and the matter of *teshuvah* is to return the lower *hei* "to its place" (as it is unified with the rest of the letters of the name *Havayah*) —a novelty is added to the "*mitzvah* of *teshuvah*," in the resolution of the heart "that he should not return, etc., to rebel against His Kingdom, may He be blessed, and he will not transgress again the command of the King, *chas v'shalom*," that even though its essence is the acceptance of the yoke regarding "turn from evil" ("that he should not return, etc., to rebel against His Kingdom, may He be blessed, and he will not transgress again the command of the King, *chas v'shalom*"), the lower *hei*, nevertheless it must be unified with the *avodos* that relate to the rest of the letters of the name *Havayah*.

And therefore the preface regarding the matter of higher *teshuvah* also relates to "the beginning of the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* and its essence," because even *teshuvah* as it is simply must be in a manner that there will be felt in it the matter of higher *teshuvah* (as mentioned in section I).

L. According to this, it is understood that the words "to explain well with an expanded explanation"—which are "corresponding to the two aspects of *teshuvah* that he mentioned afterwards, *tashuv* the lower *hei*, *tashuv* the higher *hei*" (as brought above from the notes of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe)—are not just a mere hint, but an explanation (and novelty) in the manner of doing "the beginning of the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* and its essence."

And therefore the Alter Rebbe says "to explain well with an expanded explanation by prefacing what is written in the *Zohar HaKadosh*, etc.," so that it will be clear [through the addition of the word "by prefacing"] that what he wrote "to explain well with an expanded explanation" refers not (only) to "what is written in the *Zohar HaKadosh*, etc." (as the simple meaning of the language implies), but it is (also) a matter by itself:

In order that "the beginning of the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* and its essence" should be "in truth and with a whole heart," indeed "it is necessary" that it should be in the manner hinted at in the language "to explain well with an expanded explanation."

That is to say: Even though the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* is "that he should resolve in his heart... that he should not return, etc., to rebel against His Kingdom, may He be blessed, and he will not transgress again the command of the King" ("turn from evil"), the matter of the lower *hei*, nevertheless, there must be felt in it also the *vav* —meaning, that the "to explain" must be "well," that in the resolution not to rebel against His Kingdom, may He be blessed, there must be felt (in concealment, at least) that he is prepared "to weary himself" more than his nature and habit (like the *avodah* of "do good");

And more than this—the "to explain" must be also "with an expanded explanation," "corresponding to the higher *teshuvah* of *Binah*": in the resolution there must be felt (in concealment) that he is prepared also to nullify himself and to exit entirely from his existence (like the *bitul* of engagement in Torah).

M. And with this, one can explain the reason that he hints only at the first three levels of *teshuvah*, and does not hint also at the level of "master of higher *teshuvah*" the aspect of *yud*:

Regarding the letter *yud*, they do not need a special *avodah* that it should be felt in the resolution "that he should not return, etc., to rebel against His Kingdom, may He be blessed, etc.," because the matter of the letter *yud* is (as mentioned in section G) the point of the connection (that is above form), and naturally it is understood that this point is felt in every *avodah* that is connected with the rest of the three letters, since their matter is (as mentioned in section G)—the drawing of the point into a specific form.

[And on the contrary: since the resolution not to rebel against His Kingdom, may He be blessed, is a movement of *bitul* (which is below the aspect of form), therefore specifically in it is felt the essence of the point of connection that is above form];

And since the intention of the Alter Rebbe in the words "to explain well with an expanded explanation" is to innovate how the "to return, etc." must be in practice, therefore he used such language that hints only at the first three levels.

(From a *sicha* of *Shabbos Parshas Re'eh*, 5730)


## אגרת התשובה ג

## 136

### Igeres HaTeshuvah, Chapter 3

A. In Igeres HaTeshuvah, Chapter 4, the Alter Rebbe writes: "And therefore the angels are called by the name Elokim in Scripture [and he cites three verses], as it is written, 'For Hashem your Elokim is the Elokim of the Elokim, etc.', 'Give thanks to the Elokim of the Elokim, etc.', 'And the sons of the Elokim came to present themselves, etc.', because the source of their vitality is from the aspect of the *chitzoniyus* (externality), etc., and the name Elokim is the aspect of *chitzoniyus*, etc."

In the notes of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, he explains that "he cited three verses corresponding to the three categories of angels: *serafim*, *chayos*, and *ofanim*, which are in the three worlds: *Beriah* (*serafim*), *Yetzirah* (*chayos*), and *Asiyah* (*ofanim*), and their formation is... from three categories of *osiyos* (letters) [meaning that even the letters from which the angels were formed are divided into three categories]: *machshavah* (thought) in *Beriah*, *dibbur* (speech) in *Yetzirah*, and *maaseh* (action) in *Asiyah*."
